        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer84523575" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8402016784680861946">Ah. Slow exhale. The end of the trilogy, and the final confrontation of light against dark.<br/><br/>Two contradictory reactions here: on the one hand, that was wrenching and beautiful, with intricate, soaring language to carry me through great bravery and tragedy. And I was, at one point, leaking tears as I walked down the street today. Hint: do not read the last quarter of this book in audio while going about the public portions of your day. <br/><br/>On the other hand, there is something in this book that runs c</span>
  <span id="freeText8402016784680861946" style="display:none">Ah. Slow exhale. The end of the trilogy, and the final confrontation of light against dark.<br /><br />Two contradictory reactions here: on the one hand, that was wrenching and beautiful, with intricate, soaring language to carry me through great bravery and tragedy. And I was, at one point, leaking tears as I walked down the street today. Hint: do not read the last quarter of this book in audio while going about the public portions of your day. <br /><br />On the other hand, there is something in this book that runs counter to the way I ingest stories. Take Arthur and Guinevere and Lancelot. I am on the one hand touched by the interlocked, endlessly repeating tragedy of their triangle. On the other hand, I could also be overheard to snarl, <i>oh my God, people, just have a fucking threesome. Jesus!</i><br /><br />I'm being flip, but I'm also not. Because it turns out my orientation as a reader of this kind of story – the kind that layers myth and history and tale – is deconstructive. You're all shocked, I know. And these books are not deconstructive. Nearly the opposite, actually, because Kay's project is to exult in the fundamental essences of the old stories, to find their uttermost extremities of glory and grief and write them anew, and beautifully. But to affirm them, even as he allows their endings to change a bit sometimes. And that's just not how I roll these days.<br /><br />So if you're looking for a traditional epic, and an epic <i>beautifully</i> told, then go forth. But if you're looking for something earthy and source critical, something like George R.R. Martin or maybe Abercrombie, this isn't so much the thing.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8402016784680861946" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a title="Mridupawan  Podder" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mridupawan  Podder" href="/user/show/5962024-mridupawan-podder">Mridupawan  Podder</a>

        rated it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1662429762" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1366920897099128728">And I'm done. <br/><br/>This is going to be a really, really short review. First things first, fuck you author. On to some more interesting stuff, the Darkest Road is actually a dark road for absolution, sacrifice and anything that is in the light. <br/><br/>Goodness knows I wept like a 2yo throughout this book, I had goosebumps, laughed and was drunk on euphoria, tch tch'd on a few choices and I've lived my life in Fionavar with these characters. If you're expecting a great final battle between the forces of evil </span>
  <span id="freeText1366920897099128728" style="display:none">And I'm done. <br /><br />This is going to be a really, really short review. First things first, fuck you author. On to some more interesting stuff, the Darkest Road is actually a dark road for absolution, sacrifice and anything that is in the light. <br /><br />Goodness knows I wept like a 2yo throughout this book, I had goosebumps, laughed and was drunk on euphoria, tch tch'd on a few choices and I've lived my life in Fionavar with these characters. If you're expecting a great final battle between the forces of evil and light (like the 200 page epic finale of Wheel of Time), forget it. But the skirmishes till then. Oh, it saps your strength and gives your tear ducts some good massage. <br /><br />This is a grand, grand tale of how you do the best of what you're dealt with, how you always have a choice to follow your own heart, how you sacrifice yourself for others even though the heart of your life is awaiting your victory, how you stop being a tool to be used and how you never give up on the power of light. Love stories, friendships, ego clashes and understandings all come to head in this final book when the forces of light unite for one final time to rally against the dark. <br /><br />And the dark, and the dark has a weapon no one planned for. <br /><br />Scintillating stuff.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1366920897099128728" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer15885155046647901272">This used to be one of my all time favorite books...in long..distant times, where fantasy was rare and scarce(positive person that i am, i'm hoping it still continues so when i re-read it!)<br/><br/>Of course, come to think about it, there was a lot of:<br/><br/>OM MY GOD!!   <span id="freeText15885155046647901272" style="display:none">This used to be one of my all time favorite books...in long..distant times, where fantasy was rare and scarce(positive person that i am, i'm hoping it still continues so when i re-read it!)<br><br>Of course, come to think about it, there was a lot of:<br><br>OM MY GOD!! //<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('V/4gjFyP0sMl38wI9SdH3Lox/xuzhxqWL3qyBV4J2b/MTTF0bazBU7NmNY5plUAGRNxktxHTJ/Y3Qti3LSUldg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('rMIFpSiz2fS9QXIPICxSenRlnL3h6rRgD4Qh0VAjKBU3cRRdGZDKZCv4i4m8nlWgiogHEUO+iQAXvEtjIw/U3A==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer12608734578599773513">Guy Gavriel Kay is a Canadian author of fantasy fiction. Many of his novels are set in fictional realms that resemble real places during real historical periods, such as Constantinople during the reign of Justinian I or Spain during the time of El Cid. Those works are published and marketed as historical fantasy, though the author himself has expressed a preference to shy away from genre categoriz</span>
  <span id="freeText12608734578599773513" style="display:none">Guy Gavriel Kay is a Canadian author of fantasy fiction. Many of his novels are set in fictional realms that resemble real places during real historical periods, such as Constantinople during the reign of Justinian I or Spain during the time of El Cid. Those works are published and marketed as historical fantasy, though the author himself has expressed a preference to shy away from genre categorization when possible.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12608734578599773513" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
